## Structural decisions executed

- **Valence 9 honoured.** Sustained pressure across four movements with no relief: walking party → Hannah's intelligence → Audrey's intelligence → the rumour landing in Room 412 in person.
- **The Frances Wallis-Hewitt offer** delivered exactly as canon prescribes (queer threshold via *practical* invitation, no metaphor, ambiguity preserved). The flat in Newlands, the address folded, the porter Mr Anstey, the cut key — Zeigarnik object planted; not yet used.
- **The rumour mechanism revealed as a closed loop.** The misposted Brownlow Road envelope (Ch17 peripety) is paid off by Judith's letter from Madeira — Mrs Bellingham did not open the envelope but mentioned the hand to her sister, **and her sister is Mrs Behr**, the piano teacher Hannah named at the library. The two sources Ruth identified to Hannah on the walk (the letter, the boulder) collapse into a single channel. The walk and the envelope have produced one rumour, not two.
- **The Pryce / Pryce family network specified.** The visiting Pryce (Hannah's flat) and the residence-committee Pryce (Vivienne's father) are cousins-once-removed who share a Christmas list and the Athenaeum Club in Adderley Street. Vivienne is therefore not a coincidence; she is the family's domestic instrument. Frey-compliant: the antagonist apparatus is now equal in weight to Ruth's protective apparatus (Hannah, Audrey, Eleanor, Frances, Davies).
- **Vivienne's recitation** as the chapter's terminal event. The message is delivered as a memorised sentence, not as accusation, exactly as Hannah forecast (*it will be presented as concern*). Vivienne's coda (*I did not volunteer to bring it. I did not enjoy bringing it. I do not believe what is being said about you*) is the chapter's only crack of light — and it is given to the antagonist's daughter, which is the most Frey-correct way to give it.
- **Ruth's first written record-of-conversation** is composed inside the chapter and addressed to Hannah's care, the next Tuesday. Hannah's intelligence procedure is now Ruth's procedure. The passage structurally registers Ruth as having become a person who keeps records, not just a person who is in records.
- **The desk now holds nine objects** (Tibullus letter at 9 lines, silk square open, Greek Anthology unopened, pound note in the tin, Lena's letter, William's letter, Judith's two letters, the Frances address, the Vivienne record). The Ch17 broken closing-ritual is now a chapter-by-chapter accumulation. None has been put away. The desk is becoming the chapter.
- **Closing arrest:** the porter's lamp casting a pale rectangle across the lower half of the wall opposite the window. The pines, *at last,* quiet. The mountain motif rested for once because the chapter has not been about altitude. The single italicised *at last* gives the chapter its only permitted release — and the release is silence, not resolution.

## Compliance Report

- **Punctuation & Spelling:** single quotes throughout; British spelling; zero dashes.
- **Sentence Variation:** Movement I clipped to walking-party reticence; Hannah's Movement II in the disciplined walking-rhythm now established; Audrey's Movement III in the calibrated telephone register; Vivienne's recitation as one long memorised periodic sentence followed by the three short fragments of her coda; the closing arrest in slow short paragraphs.
- **Sensory Grounding:** brown corduroy, Norfolk jacket, green enamelled flask, dark-and-faintly-bitter cold tea, Connie's chocolate squares, the cycad collection, the wet gutters of Buitenkant, Vivienne's pale grey wool cardigan and the schoolgirl confirmation hand-clasp, the Hampshire cream paper of Judith's second letter, the porter's lamp and the pale rectangle on the wall.
- **Patterns Reduced:** zero capital-quoted abstractions; zero Ruth-monologue thesis; the political weight delegated to four voices (Frances, Hannah, Audrey, Vivienne) with Ruth almost silent; the rule of three appears only inside Vivienne's coda where it is the *antagonist-daughter*'s permitted three-line confession, structurally registered.
- **Zeigarnik Applied:** loops opened — what Vivienne will say to her father; whether the warden will follow with a formal interview; whether Frances's flat in Newlands will be needed; whether the case file Hannah is now keeping will protect Ruth or expose her; whether Daniel Adams will be discharged at Pollsmoor in three weeks; whether Mrs Behr will continue to assemble the sentence; what Mrs Bellingham's exact words to her sister at supper were. Loops carried — Tibullus letter (now nine lines, still unaddressed); silk square; Greek Anthology; brisket parcel. Loops partially closed — the source of the rumour identified; Audrey informed; the residence committee's mechanism made visible.
- **Fatal Flaws Cleared:** no clichés; no perfect protagonist (Ruth's posting decision in Ch17 is now shown to have produced exactly the dramatic damage Hannah forecast; she stands at the window doing nothing for some time after Judith's letter); Vivienne not flattened to villainess but rendered as a daughter delivering an instruction she did not write; Frances given competence (the eighteen-month flat-arrangement statistic is the Frey-correct way to render a queer ally as a person who has done practical work, not as a romantic possibility); Audrey rendered as protector by procedure (*the appropriate university letterhead, sent through the registrar*).
- **Frey Compliance:** premise served (Ruth's Ruling Passion to remain precise inside collapse is being trained by being made to keep her own record); slowly rising conflict (the Pryce mechanism now formal); Ruling Passion intact (she writes the record before she sleeps); transport sequence intact (the chapter's emotional apex is the Vivienne recitation, withheld until the last scene).
- **Voice:** Frances's voice in clipped lawyerly economy; Hannah's voice in walking-rhythm; Audrey's voice in administrative calm; Vivienne's voice in the memorised-recitation register followed by the schoolgirl coda; Ruth almost silent throughout, present chiefly in the act of receiving and recording.

## Continuity / golden thread

- **Frances Wallis-Hewitt** — fourth-year law, women's law society officer, brown corduroy + grey flannel, green enamelled flask of cold tea, digs on lower Hof Street with Mr Anstey the porter and a key cut for Ruth at the address Frances handed her at the gate. Permanently named.
- **Mrs Behr** — piano teacher in the upper Gardens; Mrs Bellingham's sister; the chapter's confirmed channel from Brownlow Road to the rumour mill. Permanently named.
- **Mr Anstey** — porter at Frances's building. Permanently named.
- **Vivienne Pryce** specified as the daughter of the residence-committee Pryce, who is the cousin of the visiting (intelligence) Pryce. The Athenaeum Club in Adderley Street as the family's shared address. The two Pryces share a Christmas list. Permanently established.
- **Daniel Adams charged** with irregular residence under the Urban Areas Act, moved to Pollsmoor remand on the Saturday, hearing in three weeks, lawyer expects discharge with caution + removal order to Athlone. Available for Ch19/Ch20.
- **The Tibullus letter at 9 lines, still unaddressed.** The Greek Anthology Book V still unopened. The silk square still open on the desk. None put away. Permanent state for the desk through Ch19.
- **Ruth's first formal record of a conversation** written 13 May 1949, 6.40 p.m., addressed to herself care of Hannah for the next Tuesday. The procedure is now established and available for re-use.

## Canon flags for end-of-pass ledger

1. The single rumour-channel (Mrs Bellingham → Mrs Behr) closes the Ch17 misposting loop.
2. The Pryce family network is now disclosed as a closed circle, not two separate threats.
3. Frances Wallis-Hewitt's flat is the canonical refuge available for use in Ch19–Ch24 at any moment of acute pressure.
4. Audrey's Bellevue back bedroom is the second canonical refuge, available without ringing in advance.
5. Vivienne's coda (*I do not believe what is being said about you*) is the *only* on-page sentence of solidarity from inside the residence committee's family. Available as a small thread that may or may not survive Ch19–Ch24.
